"The Committee acknowledges that categories of\n> over-the-counter transactions, such as certain commodity swaps that may be\n> traded under the current swaps exemption, have not been excluded or\n> exempted under the terms of this Act.  The Committee intends that any\n> failure to provide a statutory exclusion or exemption for these categories\n> of swap transactions does not reflect, and should not be construed to\n> reflect, a determination by Congress that these categories of swaps\n> transactions are subject to the Commodity Exchange Act.  Also relevant is\n> pre-existing language in Section 25 that states "the provisions of this\n> section shall become effective with respect to causes of action accruing\n> on or after the date of enactment of the Futures Trading Act of 1982."\n>\n>\n> Cary Oil Co., Inc. v. MG Refining and Marketing\n> Historically, the case arises out of petroleum contracts between the\n> parties that included a pricing mechanism that allowed a counterparty to\n> blow out of the contract when the NYMEX price exceeded the contract price.\n> In hedging the transaction, MG became too exposed and word got out that\n> they were seeking to renew their long-term contracts.  The market started\n> to turn against them and ultimately, the transactions were unwound all at\n> once.   MG now alleges that those contracts were off-exchange futures\n> contracts and thus void.  At the time, NYMEX conducted an investigation\n> and a consent order was issued. Now, a second suit has been initiated in\n> which MG filed for summary judgment claiming that CFMA amendments to the\n> CEA were not retroactive.\n>\n> Federal Magistrate Judge Eaton issued a decision in a civil action the\n> week of January 7, 2002 recommending that Judge Marerro find that Section\n> 25(a)(4) (enforceability of derivatives contracts) is prospective only.\n> Specifically, Magistrate Judge Eaton held that since it was "unclear why\n> Congress chose Section 25 as the place to insert (in the CFMA) the new\n> sub-section about contract enforcement..." it should thus apply\n> prospectively only.  Thus, the consideration of Section 25(a)(4) as an\n> issue and the necessity to submit a brief supporting the retroactivity the\n> CFMA\'s non-repudiation provisions. Submitting a brief to Judge Marerro\n> would assist in emphasizing that market participants believed that this\n> issue was put to rest with the passage of the CFMA in December 2000.\n>\n>\n>\n> Stacy Carey\n> Policy Director\n> International Swaps and Derivatives Association\n> 600 5th Avenue, 27th Floor\n> Rockefeller Center\n> New York, NY  10020\n> (212) 332-1202 ph\n> (212) 332-1212 fax\n> (917) 543-9622 cell\n> scarey@isda.org\n>\n>\n>\n>', 'headings': 'Request:', 'is_duplicate': 0, 'duplicate_of': None, 'similarity_score': None, 'notification_sent': 0, 'notification_date': None, 'created_at': '2026-05-07 20:51:01'}

Sponsored by F5 Networks and produced by ITworld.com\nand Network World. http://nww1.com/go/0128F5_06.html\n\n_______________________________________________________________\nToday\'s focus: How much is too much?\n\nBy Jeb Bolding\n\nIn October I talked about Relera, which at that time, announced\nthat it was getting out of the managed-services business.\nBefore it made the announcement I visited its Internet data\ncenter in Denver and what comes to my mind when I think about\nthe discussion I had with its CEO, and my impression of the\nfacilities is one word: scale.\n\nEverything was about having the best partners, the biggest data\ncenter, massive systems redundancy rates, etc. No doubt, there\nis a place for that corporate mentality, and Relera\'s focus on\nscale should be a comfort to many enterprise companies. Relera\nmay have just been unfortunate with its timing in the market\nand it may yet be successful with its focus.\n\nAs a counterpoint, yesterday I visited another local Internet\ndata center provider, Inflow. Like Relera, Inflow is\nheadquartered in Denver, and like Relera, it is focused at\nsecond-tier cities such as Nashville and Minneapolis, though it\ndoes have some first-tier city locations.\n\nThe similarities, in my opinion, end there. Inflow\'s corporate\nesprit de corps seems to revolve around "smaller is better."\n\nAs an example, the data centers are smaller, somewhere between\n20,000 and 30,000 square feet. Not only does this bring data\ncenter profitability sooner based upon allocated space, but it\nalso gives, in the words of Inflow executives, a more personal\ntouch to the relationship between the data-center managers and\nInflow\'s customers.\n\nFurther to this point, instead of effectively building its own\nsubstations, Inflow ensures that each of its data centers\n(there are three in Denver) are located on different power\ngrids. While this may not put you in complete control over your\nown destiny, it\'s a reasonable, and cost-efficient solution\nbased upon the statistical likelihood of a disaster.\n\nWhile Inflow\'s costs are considerably less, the features of its\nfacilities do not appear to be diminished.\n\nAll data centers are mirror images of one another (other than\nthe square footage), so that a customer walking into a\nNashville facility will be just as at home in a Denver center.\n\nAll the services, from simple co-location, to managed security\nservices and monitoring, are replicated similarly across the\nvarious locations.\n\nAnd your single operational account representative is your\nfocal service point regardless of how many Inflow data centers\nyou\'re in. Management is fully integrated between the data\ncenters so that your customer representative does not have to\nbe local to your issues in order to solve them.\n\nNo doubt, there is a place in the business world for Relera and\nInflow. Inflow may have just lucked out that its focus on costs\nwill help the company better weather a long downturn.\n\n_______________________________________________________________\nTo contact Jeb Bolding:\n\nJeb Bolding is senior consultant with Enterprise Management\nAssociates in Boulder, Colo., an analyst and market research\nfirm focusing exclusively on enterprise management. As a result, there are thousands of consumers who are unable to pay their basic energy bills and the largest utility in the state is bankrupt.\n\nThe New York Times reported that you sold $101 million worth of Enron stock while aggressively urging the company's employees to keep buying it.  Please donate this money to the funds set up to help repair the lives of those Americans hurt by Enron's underhanded dealings.\n\nSincerely,\n\nBern Shen", 'body_normalized': "bern shen bernshen@earthlink.net to mr. ken lay, i'm writing to urge you to donate the millions of dollars you made from selling enron stock before the company declared bankruptcy to funds, such as enron employee transition fund and reach, that benefit the company's employees, who lost their retirement savings, and provide relief to low-income consumers in california, who can't afford to pay their energy bills. enron and you made millions out of the pocketbooks of california consumers and from the efforts of your employees. indeed, while you netted well over a $100 million, many of enron's employees were financially devastated when the company declared bankruptcy and their retirement plans were wiped out. and enron made an astronomical profit during the california energy crisis last year. as a result, there are thousands of consumers who are unable to pay their basic energy bills and the largest utility in the state is bankrupt. the new york times reported that you sold $101 million worth of enron stock while aggressively urging the company's employees to keep buying it. please donate this money to the funds set up to help repair the lives of those americans hurt by enron's underhanded dealings. sincerely, bern shen", 'body_hash': '86bb5edca174bc914e730b27c5085083', 'source_file': 'lay-k/deleted_items/107.', 'x_from': '"bernshen@earthlink.net" <bernshen@earthlink.net>@ENRON', 'x_to': 'klay@enron.com', 'x_cc': None, 'x_bcc': None, 'x_folder': '\\Kenneth_Lay_Mar2002\\Lay, Kenneth\\Deleted Items', 'x_origin': 'Lay-K', 'content_type': 'text/plain', 'has_attachment': 0, 'forwarded_content': None, 'quoted_content': None, 'headings': None, 'is_duplicate': 0, 'duplicate_of': None, 'similarity_score': None, 'notification_sent': 0, 'notification_date': None, 'created_at': '2026-05-07 20:49:16'}
